## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This is a chemical reaction kinetics problem where the rate of concentration change dA_dt depends on the current concentration A and possibly time t. The relationship encodes the rate law of the reaction, which could range from simple power-law kinetics to more complex mechanisms involving reversibility, autocatalysis, or time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Reversible second-order/first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression from reversible mechanism)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction where product relates to A)
- Logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (autocatalytic with saturation)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (mixed mechanism yielding fractional order)
- Time-modulated first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant)
- Saturation kinetics (Lindemann-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A) (pressure-dependent unimolecular decomposition)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A + c3 (complex multi-step mechanism)
- Square-root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (dissociative equilibrium followed by reaction)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (substrate inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical rate law dA_dt = f(A), indicating an autonomous ODE from elementary or lumped reaction steps
- Polynomial in A → suggests a reaction mechanism with multiple elementary steps that have been combined into an overall rate expression
- Fractional/non-integer power of A → indicates a complex mechanism where intermediates have been eliminated via steady-state or equilibrium approximations
- Rational function of A (ratio of polynomials) → Lindemann-type or enzyme-like mechanism with competing pathways
- Explicit time dependence → non-autonomous system, possibly from time-varying external conditions (temperature ramp, light intensity) or elimination of another species' concentration expressed as function of t
- Sign of dA_dt determines whether A is a reactant (negative rate) or product (positive rate) — constrains the sign of leading coefficients
- A*(1-A) or A*(c-A) structure → conservation law where total concentration is fixed, typical of A↔B reversible reactions
- Multiple roots in dA_dt=0 as function of A → multiple steady states, characteristic of bistable or autocatalytic systems

**GT:** `-0.33236*A**2 - 0.33236*A*exp(-0.07071*t) + 0.13650*sin(sqrt(A))`

The key term here is `sin(sqrt(A))`. This is a very specific nonlinear function that cannot be represented by polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or power functions of A. Let me check if any candidate contains `sin(sqrt(A))` or an equivalent.

Looking through all 55 candidates, I see the following types of nonlinear terms:
- `log(A*c + 1)` - logarithmic terms
- `exp(A*c)` - exponential in A
- `(A + 1)**(1/3)` or `(A + c)**c` - power terms

- `1/(A + c)**n` - rational terms

The critical question is: can `sin(sqrt(A))` be expressed using any combination of the available building blocks?

This is an infinite series in half-integer powers of A. No finite combination of the terms available in any candidate (polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, power functions with fixed or free exponents) can exactly equal `sin(sqrt(A))` for all A ≥ 0.
